  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

  <span id="freeText4989251821982105870" style="display:none">Up into the cherry tree<br />Who should climb but little me?<br />I held the trunk with both my hands<br />And looked abroad on foreign lands.<br /><br />Here is a delightful look at childhood, written by master poet and storyteller Robert Louis Stevenson. In this collection of sixty-six poems, Stevenson recalls the joys of his childhood, from sailing boats down a river, to waiting for the lamplighter, to sailing off to foreign lands in his imagination.<br /><br />Tasha Tudor's watercolour paintings evoke a simpler time in the past, and celebrate two of the things she loves most — children and nature. Her talents are the perfect match for these inspiring poems, making this a handsome gift edition that will be cherished by families for generations.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2682238504" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2682238504" />
    <a title="Cecily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1199525-cecily"><img alt="Cecily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480285828p2/1199525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2682238504?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cecily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cecily" href="/user/show/1199525-cecily">Cecily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780192760326" href="/book/show/2845710-a-child-s-garden-of-verses">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=art">art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2682238504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5181697882357539077">"<i>Everything was grey. There wasn't any colour. It was all up to my imagination.</i>”<br/>Brian Wildsmith, artist, on his childhood.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548592611i/26976419._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>Image</b>: <i>Summer Sun</i><br/><br/>This review is an excuse to share some of the startling and colourful illustrations that Wildsmith crafted for this 1966 edition (words <a href='http://www.gutenberg.org/cache/epub/136/pg136-images.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>). A truly wild smith. I can’t imagine what Robert Louis Stevenson would make of them, but I hope he would appreciate the edge they give to his words.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548592611i/26976420._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>Image</b>: <i>The Cow</i><br/>The poem leaves me cold, but the happy cow in her bucolic</span>
  <span id="freeText5181697882357539077" style="display:none">"<i>Everything was grey. There wasn't any colour. It was all up to my imagination.</i>”<br>Brian Wildsmith, artist, on his childhood.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548592611i/26976419._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>Summer Sun</i><br><br>This review is an excuse to share some of the startling and colourful illustrations that Wildsmith crafted for this 1966 edition (words <a href="http://www.gutenberg.org/cache/epub/136/pg136-images.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>). A truly wild smith. I can’t imagine what Robert Louis Stevenson would make of them, but I hope he would appreciate the edge they give to his words.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548592611i/26976420._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>The Cow</i><br>The poem leaves me cold, but the happy cow in her bucolic meadow, I love. <br><br>The poems are mostly delightful. Many are familiar from repetition in my childhood, then to my child. We had plenty of other books of rhymes, but it was primarily the extravagant illustrations that drew me repeatedly to the pages, and the words I learned so well.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548592611i/26976421._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>The Land of the Counterpane</i><br>I think this made me something of a hypochondriac as a child - though I’m quite the reverse as an adult.<br><br>When I’ve seen modern editions, they’re invariably illustrated with competent, sometimes lovely pictures, but they're safe and predictable. Just what you expect for a cosy Victorian classic. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548592611i/26976422._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>Armies in the Fire</i><br>I loved pareidolia long before I knew there was a word for it; perhaps this is why?<br><br>I think the dissonance of Wildsmith’s pictures and Stevenson's verses add the vibrant joy and confusing kaleidoscope of childhood, and sometimes add modern relevance to the words themselves.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548592611i/26976423._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>Whole Duty of Children</i><br>A dry Victorian instruction with a subversive twist.<br><br>The child is always clearly recognisable, a character to identify with, but the backgrounds are often more abstract. There are echoes of Klimt, Turner, Miro, and Matisse, yet they are very much Wildsmith’s own.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548592611i/26976424._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>Looking-Glass River</i><br>An example where the words do little for me, but the picture is lush.<br><br><b>My Favourite</b><br><br>I was a tomboy, who loved cars, tractors, and trains. This was my favourite poem, and as an adult, I think the words, rhythm, and imagery are superb. You can't read it slowly, nor should you:<br><br><blockquote>Faster than fairies, faster than witches,<br> Bridges and houses, hedges and ditches;<br> And charging along like troops in a battle<br> All through the meadows the horses and cattle:<br> All of the sights of the hill and the plain<br> Fly as thick as driving rain;<br> And ever again, in the wink of an eye,<br> Painted stations whistle by.<br><br> Here is a child who clambers and scrambles,<br> All by himself and gathering brambles;<br> Here is a tramp who stands and gazes;<br> And here is the green for stringing the daisies!<br> Here is a cart run away in the road<br> Lumping along with man and load;<br> And here is a mill, and there is a river:<br> Each a glimpse and gone forever!</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548592611i/26976425._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>From a Railway Carriage</i><br><br>Then I went to Tate Britain for the first of many times (probably around seven years old) and saw this. The two are forever, happily, linked in my mind:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1548592611i/26976426._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>Rain, Steam and Speed - The Great Western Railway, by JMW Turner</i><br><br><b>The Verses</b><br><br>See Ted's excellent review, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2680910270" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>, which is what prompted me to get out my copy and post this. <br><br>All the poems are free on Gutenberg, <a href="http://www.gutenberg.org/cache/epub/136/pg136-images.html" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5181697882357539077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1256535360" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1256535360" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1256535360?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=children-of-all-ages">children-of-all-ages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=1-star-reads">1-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1256535360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10937851260564155010"><i> A Child's Garden of Verses</i> is a collection of poetry aimed at young children though due to the latent racism and views on British supremacy, I would not recommend it to a young impressionable reader. <br/><br/>Robert Louis Stevenson was a very versatile writer; he delved deep into the human psyche when he wrote <i>The Strange Case of Doctor Jekyll and Mr Hyde</i> but he did not restrict himself to representations of the gothic and the persecuted. He also wrote brilliant children's adventure stories such as <i>Trea</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10937851260564155010" style="display:none"><i> A Child's Garden of Verses</i> is a collection of poetry aimed at young children though due to the latent racism and views on British supremacy, I would not recommend it to a young impressionable reader. <br /><br />Robert Louis Stevenson was a very versatile writer; he delved deep into the human psyche when he wrote <i>The Strange Case of Doctor Jekyll and Mr Hyde</i> but he did not restrict himself to representations of the gothic and the persecuted. He also wrote brilliant children's adventure stories such as <i>Treasure Island</i> and <i>Kidnapped</i>, but, again, he did not restrict himself to prose writing because here he demonstrates his ability to write poetry.<br /><br />In the fashion of William Blake's <i>The Songs of Innocence and Experience</i>, Stevenson's poetry has a certain deceptive quality. Like Blake's writing, it looks very simple on the surface. The style employed hides the nature of the poetry. The diction is very straight forward, but if you scratch the surface of the poetry and consider the meanings of the words in a wider context you will see exactly what I mean. It is very important to note the era in which Stevenson wrote these verses; he was a Victorian and as such there are some latent views regarding race that would be considered slightly risqué by today's standards.<br /><br />For example Stevenson celebrates British identity with an attempt at humour, though unfortunately it is at the expense at everything foreign. I would hesitate to recommend this book to children due to the nature of its representations of everything not British. Instead a more mature discerning reader is required to sieve through the falsities of Stevenson's representations, and to understand that he is not entirely to blame for them: he, like all the Victorians, wrote from a position of ignorance towards the east. They believed Britain Empire was the absolute apex of culture and society, everything else by comparison was lesser and underdeveloped. Their view of the world was distorted to say the least.<br /><br />This edition here if full of colourful illustrations that sit perfectly with the apparent simplicity of the poetry; it, certainly, is very pleasant to look upon. But, again, I would not put this in the hand of a child today because of the nature of some of the poems. A young reader could very easily absorb the information here, information that provides the views and opinions of a mind-set out of date and completely out of touch with the realities of Empire. This, in itself, is a real shame because there are some good pieces of poetry in here, but when Stevenson addresses the foreign he does so with the haughtiness and pomposity that came with his own literary era.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10937851260564155010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2680910270" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2680910270" />
    <a title="Ted" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7213075-ted"><img alt="Ted" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553101210p2/7213075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2680910270?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ted" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ted" href="/user/show/7213075-ted">Ted</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7213075-ted?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7213075-ted?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7213075-ted?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2680910270" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7489245592931977248"><b>just got this book. I've read a few of the poems, but it really isn't for me.<br/>I'll soon be giving it to my daughter. It's for <i>her</i> daughter, my seven-year old granddaughter.<br/><br/>It turns out that the youngster is currently enamored with poetry. Her bedtime reading of choice, her reading of choice <i>period</i> - meaning what she reads on her own.<br/><br/>It's interesting. None of her family have that interest except me, and I only got the poetry bug a few years ago.<br/><br/>Probably has to due with a poetry splurge by her teac</b></span>
  <span id="freeText7489245592931977248" style="display:none"><b>just got this book. I've read a few of the poems, but it really isn't for me.<br />I'll soon be giving it to my daughter. It's for <i>her</i> daughter, my seven-year old granddaughter.<br /><br />It turns out that the youngster is currently enamored with poetry. Her bedtime reading of choice, her reading of choice <i>period</i> - meaning what she reads on her own.<br /><br />It's interesting. None of her family have that interest except me, and I only got the poetry bug a few years ago.<br /><br />Probably has to due with a poetry splurge by her teacher. Anyway, I'm sure she will love this book</b><br /><br />. . . . . . . . . . . .<br /><br /><br />My review resulted from a look at a couple of A.A. Milne's books here on the site. And that resulted from This Day in History for Jan. 18, in which the birth of A.A. on that date in 1882 was indicated. <br /><br />This led to a mention by Goodreads of a similar book, the one being reviewed.<br /><br />Now, I can't be sure how much of this book I've read. I thought we once had it in the house, which my wife verified. But a search in all the likely places didn't turn it up.<br /><br />Well, Robert Louis Stevenson. Most noted for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/295.Treasure_Island" title="Treasure Island by Robert Louis Stevenson" rel="nofollow noopener">Treasure Island</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/325128.Kidnapped__David_Balfour___1_" title="Kidnapped (David Balfour, #1) by Robert Louis Stevenson" rel="nofollow noopener">Kidnapped</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51496.The_Strange_Case_of_Dr__Jekyll_and_Mr__Hyde" title="The Strange Case of Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde by Robert Louis Stevenson" rel="nofollow noopener">Strange Case of Dr Jekyll and Mr Hyde</a>, and <i>A Child's Garden of Verses</i>. To my memory, he is most noted for the epitaph that he wanted inscribed on his tomb.<blockquote>Under the wide and starry sky,<br />Dig the grave and let me lie.<br />Glad did I live and gladly die,<br />And I laid me down with a will.<br />This be the verse you grave for me:<br />Here he lies where he longed to be;<br />Home is the sailor, home from sea,<br />And the hunter home from the hill.</blockquote>I no longer can be sure of why these words have lodged into my memory. I vaguely recollect that they were quoted as an epigraph in some short story (possibly a SF story) read long ago.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Well a search on that turned up a story by Robert Heinlein called <i>Requiem</i>. It's the lead story in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1381155.Famous_Science_Fiction_Stories_Adventures_in_Time_and_Space" title="Famous Science-Fiction Stories Adventures in Time and Space by Raymond J. Healy" rel="nofollow noopener">Famous Science Fiction Stories Adventures in Time and Space</a>. My copy is a Modern Library Giant published in 1957. I might guess that I bought it and read that first story in high school. Thanks for the memory, Modern Library!<br /><br />The Stephenson thing isn't an epigraph. It's right up front in the story itself.<blockquote>On a high hill in Samoa there is a grave. Inscribed on the marker are these words:<blockquote>(…the Stephenson thing…)</blockquote>These lines appear another place – scrawled on a shipping tag torn from a compressed-air cylinder, and pinned to the ground with a knife.</blockquote>And away Heinlein goes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Stevenson went through a long period of decline in the 20th century. His Wiki article gives examples to document that he came to be judged a second-rate writer, to the extent that in the 1973 2,000-page Oxford Anthology of English Literature he was entirely unmentioned. Since then his reputation has rebounded quite a bit:<blockquote>The late 20th century brought a re-evaluation of Stevenson as an artist of great range and insight, a literary theorist, an essayist and social critic, a witness to the colonial history of the Pacific Islands, and a humanist. He was praised by Roger Lancelyn Green, one of the Oxford Inklings, as a writer of a consistently high level of "literary skill or sheer imaginative power" and a pioneer of the Age of the Story Tellers along with H. Rider Haggard. He is now evaluated as a peer of authors such as Joseph Conrad (whom Stevenson influenced with his South Seas fiction) and Henry James, with new scholarly studies and organizations devoted to him.</blockquote> Throughout the century however, Stevenson remained widely popular. One index ranks him as the 26th most translated author in the world, ahead of Oscar Wilde and Edgar Allan Poe.<br /><br />Here's a couple poems from <i>Garden</i>.<br /><br /><b>The Lamplighter</b><br /><br />My tea is nearly ready and the sun has left the sky;<br />It's time to take the window to see Leerie going by;<br />For every night at teatime and before you take your seat,<br />With lantern and with ladder he comes posting up the street.<br />Now Tom would be a driver and Maria go to sea,<br />And my papa's a banker and as rich as he can be;<br />But I, when I am stronger and can choose what I'm to do,<br />O Leerie, I'll go round at night and light the lamps with you!<br />For we are very lucky, with a lamp before the door,<br />And Leerie stops to light it as he lights so many more;<br />And O! before you hurry by with ladder and with light,<br />O Leerie, see a little child and nod to him tonight!<br /><br /><br /><b>My Shadow</b><br /><br />I have a little shadow that goes in and out with me,<br />And what can be the use of him is more than I can see.<br />He is very, very like me from the heels up to the head;<br />And I see him jump before me, when I jump into my bed.<br /><br />The funniest thing about him is the way he likes to grow—<br />Not at all like proper children, which is always very slow;<br />For he sometimes shoots up taller like an India-rubber ball,<br />And he sometimes gets so little that there's none of him at all.<br /><br />He hasn't got a notion of how children ought to play,<br />And can only make a fool of me in every sort of way.<br />He stays so close beside me, he's a coward you can see;<br />I'd think shame to stick to nursie as that shadow sticks to me!<br /><br />One morning, very early, before the sun was up,<br />I rose and found the shining dew on every buttercup;<br />But my lazy little shadow, like an errant sleepy-head,<br />Had stayed at home behind me and was fast asleep in bed.<br /><br /><b>The rating - well, a lot of my friends have given it the same, that's good enough for me.</b><br /><br /><br />. . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . .<br /><b>Previous review:</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2513029271" rel="nofollow noopener">The Corpse Exhibition</a><br /><b>Next review:</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2396462915" rel="nofollow noopener">The Supplicants</a> <i>Aeschylus</i><br /><b>Older review:</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/715377465" rel="nofollow noopener">The Glory of their Times</a><br /><br /><b>Previous library review:</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/248907443" rel="nofollow noopener">Far From the Madding Crowd</a><br /><b>Next library review:</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1268299169" rel="nofollow noopener">One Fat Englishman</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7489245592931977248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_317102072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317102072" />
    <a title="Soraya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8972144-soraya"><img alt="Soraya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335215946p2/8972144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/317102072?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Soraya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Soraya" href="/user/show/8972144-soraya">Soraya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317102072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer577770401395420916">My grandma gave me this book when I was very young. I read it around ages 6-7 years-old. It made me happy to be young and now it makes me want to be that young again. It was strange how easily I could identify with the young Robert Louis Stevenson. I could absolutely understand his annoyance at being sent to bed while it was still light in summer and I just wanted to be there with him. When I read it back now I am reminded of the innocence of being so young, something that I didn't think about o</span>
  <span id="freeText577770401395420916" style="display:none">My grandma gave me this book when I was very young. I read it around ages 6-7 years-old. It made me happy to be young and now it makes me want to be that young again. It was strange how easily I could identify with the young Robert Louis Stevenson. I could absolutely understand his annoyance at being sent to bed while it was still light in summer and I just wanted to be there with him. When I read it back now I am reminded of the innocence of being so young, something that I didn't think about on first reading because I was far to innocent to understand innocence. I am baffled that a poetry book first released in 1885 could capture the imagination of a 7 year-old girl in 2002. That makes it unique in my view. <br />In childish writing, inside the cover of my copy it says 'This book was given to me by Grandma Bertha.' My Grandma Bertha has since passed away and this is the most treasured thing I have that she gave to me. It was the first time I had loved reading poetry and it probably first sparked my interest in poetry as a genre. This book is brilliant. Buy it for your children or grand children. I'm very glad my Grandma Bertha did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="577770401395420916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_87797546" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87797546" />
    <a title="max" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3225020-max"><img alt="max" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470021463p2/3225020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87797546?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="max" class="user" itemprop="url" name="max" href="/user/show/3225020-max">max</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3225020-max?shelf=childrens-books">childrens-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87797546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17799369673164531456">The Land of Counterpane<br/><br/>When I was sick and lay a-bed, <br/>I had two pillows at my head, <br/>And all my toys beside me lay, <br/>To keep me happy all the day. <br/><br/> * * * * *<br/><br/>I was the giant great and still <br/>That sits upon the pillow-hill, <br/>And sees before him, dale and plain, <br/>The pleasant land of counterpane.<br/><br/>Once upon a time, when I was a young child home sick from school and confined to bed, my mother encouraged me to memorize this poem. The title baffled me, since I had no idea what a counterpane was. I thought th</span>
  <span id="freeText17799369673164531456" style="display:none">The Land of Counterpane<br /><br />When I was sick and lay a-bed, <br />I had two pillows at my head, <br />And all my toys beside me lay, <br />To keep me happy all the day. <br /><br /> * * * * *<br /><br />I was the giant great and still <br />That sits upon the pillow-hill, <br />And sees before him, dale and plain, <br />The pleasant land of counterpane.<br /><br />Once upon a time, when I was a young child home sick from school and confined to bed, my mother encouraged me to memorize this poem. The title baffled me, since I had no idea what a counterpane was. I thought that perhaps it had some connection with a windowpane. Only years later when I looked the word up did I discover that it was a bedspread. I can still recall the captivatingly beautiful illustration that accompanied the poem -- a young boy in bed looking rather unwell with little houses and toy soldiers surrounding him. And so I tackled the project of memorizing it, reading the lines, getting the words into my head, using the rhyme scheme to lock it firmly into place. By day's end I could recite the full poem, all sixteen lines of its four stanzas.<br /><br />We had one of those delightful large anthologies of children's poems and stories (including several from A Child's Garden of Verses) and I recall things like "Animal crackers and cocoa to drink" (first line of a poem by Christopher Morley) and also the story of The Little Match Girl in the same volume. Do they even publish these anymore? More to the point, would children read them if they did? The book opened up another world, one which, in my solitude, I was all too happy to enter. This kind of book was for me a precious treasure. The notion of watching television was unthinkable, as my mother would not have allowed it. And really, for intellectual stimulation and aesthetic experience, what television program could possibly have matched my intimate encounter with R.L. Stevenson on that particular morning?<br /><br />We are now at the stage where the intrusion of technology into our lives -- especially the lives of children -- can properly be called into question. When you memorize a poem, you own it. It takes mental effort, of course, and the slow task of building the complete product in your head also requires considerable patience. Technology, such as cellphones with instantaneous internet access, removes any need for effort or for patience. Something precious is lost in the process. Alas, when the imaginative life shrivels and dies, civilization dies along with it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17799369673164531456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7125762136026201893" style="display:none">Now I will be the first to admit that, limericks, verse and poetry are not my strengths and I am happy with that however as I work my way through the Everyman Children's Library I am trying to open myself up to new books and experiences. <br /><br />And so I came to Robert Louis Stevenson's book of garden verses - I am not sure why it is has reference to garden it in as honestly it covers all mater of subjects but it is primarily focused on children and the view on the world. <br /><br />Now there are so I recognise in this book there are so I think I should recognise but I realise I do not and there is plenty here for me to learn. <br /><br />As with the other books in this series it takes its illustrations from its most famous and most prominent edition and as such is all the more special for it (I really love the other books in the series illustrated by W Heath-Robinson) So yes I am not sure if I would claim to have read this book if it were not for its significance however I know I am better for having done so</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42315986-hilary?shelf=seasons">seasons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42315986-hilary?shelf=male-author-or-illustrator">male-author-or-illustrator</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42315986-hilary?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1560535810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10559513743425084071">This rates 5 stars for the beautiful illustrations by Eve Garnet alone, the poems are lovely too, although some of the statements about children will sound dated to the modern ear, there are some lovely evocative words and pictures of idyllic childhoods and country scenes. I have a 1940s copy of this book that I spent many happy hours as a child reading or tracing the pictures so I could paint colour into the beautiful line drawings.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1238591977" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1238591977" />
    <a title="Gerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1525599-gerry"><img alt="Gerry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580749249p2/1525599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1238591977?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gerry" href="/user/show/1525599-gerry">Gerry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1238591977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7996423459582819097">One could argue that Robert Louis Stevenson's 'A Child's Garden of Verses' is one of the best children's poetry books ever written. There are so many poems evocative of childhood that will bring back memories for many readers and reading these poems aloud - even to oneself - is an absolute delight.<br/><br/>Even the poem in dedication to his nurse Alison Cunningham is divine with lines such as 'And grant it, Heaven, that all you need/May find as dear a nurse at need/...May hear it in as kind a voice/As ma</span>
  <span id="freeText7996423459582819097" style="display:none">One could argue that Robert Louis Stevenson's 'A Child's Garden of Verses' is one of the best children's poetry books ever written. There are so many poems evocative of childhood that will bring back memories for many readers and reading these poems aloud - even to oneself - is an absolute delight.<br /><br />Even the poem in dedication to his nurse Alison Cunningham is divine with lines such as 'And grant it, Heaven, that all you need/May find as dear a nurse at need/...May hear it in as kind a voice/As made my childish days rejoice!'<br />The opening poem is rather dramatic, 'Windy Nights' beginning 'Whenever the moon and stars are set,/Whenever the wind is high,'All nght long in the dark and the wet,/A man goes riding by./Late in the night when the fires are out,/Why does he gallop and gallop about?' And the following poem moves swiftly on to 'Bed in Summer', a much more tranquil scene that ends with something most children may ask, 'And does it not seem hard to you,/When all the sky is clear and blue,/And I should like so much to play,/To have to go to bed by day?' Yes, indeed it does, or it did when I was young!<br /><br />RLS visits 'Foreign Lands' that 'Lead onward into Fairyland', looks surprisingly at 'My Shadow' that from being huge 'Had stayed at home behind me and was fast asleep in bed', loves the air whizzing by on 'The Swing' as 'Up in the air I go flying again,/Up in the air and down' and admires 'Nest Eggs' 'While we stand watching her/Staring like gabies,/Safe in the eggs are the/Bird's little babies'.<br /><br />He sees 'The Wind' with 'I saw you toss the kites on high,/And blow the birds across the sky;/And all around I heard you pass,/Like ladies' skirts across the grass -/O wind, a-blowing all day long,/O wind, that sings sop loud a song!' And the end poem 'To My Name-child' has the lovely lines, 'Some day soon this rhyming volume, if you learn with proper speed,/Little Louis Sanchez, will be given you to read' - of course, any name can be substituted for LS - and it will delight any child that picks it up.<br /><br />'A Child's Garden of Verses' - in any edition - is one to be read and enjoyed, reliving childhood memories, over and over again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7996423459582819097" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1522863037" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1522863037" />
    <a title="Velma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1843025-velma"><img alt="Velma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1287255581p2/1843025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1522863037?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Velma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Velma" href="/user/show/1843025-velma">Velma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780688145842" href="/book/show/4276066-a-child-s-garden-of-verses">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">parents, children, and all who have ever been one or the other</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Velma by: </span>
      found a copy at my local support-the-library sale
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1843025-velma?shelf=childrens-kids">childrens-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1843025-velma?shelf=brit-lit">brit-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1843025-velma?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1843025-velma?shelf=victoriana">victoriana</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1843025-velma?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1843025-velma?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1522863037" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7207901812596704588">Strung these poems end to end like beads on a string around my heart, reading slowly to savor. Exquisite! Not all resonate with a modern reader: most espouse adherence to traditional gender roles; almost all take as their subject the joys and tragedies of childhood experiences, and quite a few are sadly now relegated to a bygone era and will therefore be unfamiliar to many readers (like nurses and nannies for children, candles to light a path to bed at night, and typical rural life staples like </span>
  <span id="freeText7207901812596704588" style="display:none">Strung these poems end to end like beads on a string around my heart, reading slowly to savor. Exquisite! Not all resonate with a modern reader: most espouse adherence to traditional gender roles; almost all take as their subject the joys and tragedies of childhood experiences, and quite a few are sadly now relegated to a bygone era and will therefore be unfamiliar to many readers (like nurses and nannies for children, candles to light a path to bed at night, and typical rural life staples like mills and haylofts); and at times they are tinged with the slightly xenophobic Brit/Western perspective of the Victorian Era in which they were penned. But it is all no matter! These classic "children's" poems nonetheless delighted me, because at the heart of each verse is magic and make believe, still alive and well in children of all ages today. Replete with pirates and imaginary friends, dreams in the day as well as the night, and "valiant battles lost and won".<br /><br />Although I have no memories of hearing these as a child, nor reading them myself (despite being an early reader, unlike Stevenson who surprisingly didn't learn how to navigate books until he was about 7 years old), many of them are nonetheless comfortingly familiar to me, while others are new-to-me gems. Along with the perennial obvious favorites like <i>The Land of Counterpane</i>, <i>Rain</i>, <i>My Shadow</i>, and <i>The Land of Nod</i>, I particularly love the travelers tales, like <i>Historical Associations</i> and <i>To Minnie</i>; the garden delight verse <i>The Little Land</i> "Where the clover tops are trees/And the rain pools are the seas"; and the poems extolling books, <i>Picture Books in Winter</i> and <i>The Land of Storybooks</i>. But my absolute favorite is <i>Block City</i>, in which a child creates a fabled world inside the house on a rainy day.<br /><br />The edition I read, illustrated by Caldecott-winner Diane Goode, contains over 70 color and black-and-white illustrations that are balanced from a gender and racial standpoint, which I particularly like. And, they are lovely without being overly sentimental. <br /><br />A note on language: I read one or two reviews complaining about the archaic vocabulary used in <i>A Child's Garden of Verses</i>, and I'd like to speak to that. I recently read, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/289751.Proust_and_the_Squid_The_Story_and_Science_of_the_Reading_Brain" title="Proust and the Squid The Story and Science of the Reading Brain by Maryanne Wolf" rel="nofollow noopener">Proust and the Squid: The Story and Science of the Reading Brain</a> by Maryanne Wolf, of a 1995 study that showed that American children growing up in "underprivileged" and "linguistically impoverished" homes (ie., families in which reading, singing, and talking to young children is not emphasized) are exposed by the age of five to, on average, 32 MILLION fewer words than their more "stimulated" peers. That 32 million word gap in the vocabulary of underprivileged children is so detrimental that they are already at an educational disadvantage by the time they reach kindergarten. And, as I'm sure all Goodreaders know, illiteracy is predictive of many of the "social ills" in American society, including crime, incarceration rates, and poverty. According to Wolf:<br /><br /><blockquote>Children who never have a story read to them, who never hear words that rhyme, who never imagine fighting with dragons or marrying a prince, have the odds overwhelmingly against them."</blockquote><br />So to those that are put off by the seemingly outmoded lexicon of <i>A Child's Garden of Verses</i>, think of it instead as a great way to get a jump on that 32 million word gap we should all want to avoid. Viva la dictionary!<br /><br />Finally, let's hear from RLS himself, in one of the shortest verses from the book:<br /><br /><blockquote>Happy Thought<br /><br />The world is so full of a number of things,<br />I'm sure we should all be as happy as kings.</blockquote><br />I don't know about you, but in a world as full of ugliness as ours, this admonition to remember how full the world is of happy-making things does my heart good and seems a perfect place to end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7207901812596704588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_213399241" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/213399241" />
    <a title="Cher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6410740-cher"><img alt="Cher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316737029p2/6410740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/213399241?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cher" href="/user/show/6410740-cher">Cher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6410740-cher?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6410740-cher?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6410740-cher?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer213399241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8445841722842136947">This is a sentimental review because of how personally I cherish this collection. My grandfather had a old edition of this book like from the 1940s and whenever my sister and I slept over, he would read the different poems over and over again until we fell asleep. So to say I adore this book is a bit of an understatement as I can't read the poems without hearing my grandpa's voice. The poems themselves are utterly charming, harking back to an older childhood, perhaps a more innocent one, a time </span>
  <span id="freeText8445841722842136947" style="display:none">This is a sentimental review because of how personally I cherish this collection. My grandfather had a old edition of this book like from the 1940s and whenever my sister and I slept over, he would read the different poems over and over again until we fell asleep. So to say I adore this book is a bit of an understatement as I can't read the poems without hearing my grandpa's voice. The poems themselves are utterly charming, harking back to an older childhood, perhaps a more innocent one, a time when television, internet, and wii were not around to mindlessly entertain a young mind. Instead they are a reminder about what childhood used to mean, possibly the idealistic memories adults think they had of their childhood, but I still like to give this as a gift to young children as I hope it will inspire them to turn off their electronics and relish in their play and imagination as they once did. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8445841722842136947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1232879592" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Malakai Kong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Malakai Kong" href="/user/show/24614836-malakai-kong">Malakai Kong</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1232879592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3026261569168467068">"The Wind" by Robert Louis Stevenson is a rhyming poem. It talks about the wind and how it feels.<br/><br/>My favorite line is, "O you that are so strong and cold." It makes me feel like the wind will blow me off my feet! My favorite rhyming words are "cold and old," "sky and high," and "long and song."<br/><br/>I think the poet wrote this poem on a windy day. He may have gone outside and then written this poem to describe how he feels about the wind.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2392764844" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2392764844" />
    <a title="Jo Walton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3350560-jo-walton"><img alt="Jo Walton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333431622p2/3350560.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2392764844?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo Walton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo Walton" href="/user/show/3350560-jo-walton">Jo Walton</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18871460-a-child-s-garden-of-verses">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2392764844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8808764503876212858">Delightful poems, exactly to a child's experience and taste, and surprisingly unproblematic considering their age. A parent might want to explain to a child that "negro" was the normal polite term for Africans when RLS wrote but it isn't now, and that's about it, and you can explain it in the same way you explain why we don't dress by candle-light and have nurses any more. <br/><br/>Perhaps these are too formative for me to have a rational opinion.<br/><br/>When I was a kid, reading these, I was convinced that RLS </span>
  <span id="freeText8808764503876212858" style="display:none">Delightful poems, exactly to a child's experience and taste, and surprisingly unproblematic considering their age. A parent might want to explain to a child that "negro" was the normal polite term for Africans when RLS wrote but it isn't now, and that's about it, and you can explain it in the same way you explain why we don't dress by candle-light and have nurses any more. <br /><br />Perhaps these are too formative for me to have a rational opinion.<br /><br />When I was a kid, reading these, I was convinced that RLS had written them when he was in fact himself still a child, that unlike everything else I read that was written for adults for children or for adults for other adults, these poems alone were written by a child for children, from a child's real and present experience. Reading it now, I can entirely see why I thought that, and I still almost think it, even though I know better. Like RLS I was a child who had to spend time in bed sick, who liked to play outside, and a lot of these experiences of considering scale and the world still ring very true -- but maybe because I read them so young and internalised them. The difference in length and rhyme scheme of these poems still seems to me exactly to a child's taste and utterly different from the way an adult would shape them. An adult wouldn't write "The world is so full of a number of things I'm sure we should all be as happy as kings" and leave it as that, as the whole poem, which has been giving me satisfaction for half a century. But Stevenson did, and I'm glad he did.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8808764503876212858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17049356041647421260">My edition different cover, with an assortment of classic illustrations chosen by Cooper Edens.<br/>My review from the Children's Books discussion for Poetry month:<br/><br/>Emphasizes the sentimental and the nostalgic.   <span id="freeText17049356041647421260" style="display:none">My edition different cover, with an assortment of classic illustrations chosen by Cooper Edens.<br />My review from the Children's Books discussion for Poetry month:<br /><br />Emphasizes the sentimental and the nostalgic. That may be appropriate, and a good way to sell the book to the ppl with the money... but I'm not sure if it helps today's children appreciate the timelessness of the verses.<br /><br />I would have loved any edition of this when my children were tiny. Reading it now, I feel as if I deprived my kids!<br /><br />Even nursing infants could appreciate the sounds, the rhythm, rhyme, and alliteration of the poems as read aloud. It won't be long before some of the lines stick in their heads... even if they don't understand them.<br /><br />And toddlers can enjoy many of the concepts... and preschoolers more... and some of the poems are worth a teen student's time. Owning whichever edition of this you prefer is like owning a big book of Mother Goose rhymes, and another big book, or collection, of famous fairy tales... it's almost a must!<br /><br />Many of the poems have been reprinted in other collections, including the Nat'l Geog. we read upthread. But many are new to me, too. </span>

<div id="review_292272563" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="GoldGato" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6401606-goldgato"><img alt="GoldGato" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407995357p2/6401606.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780894717154" href="/book/show/986661.A_Child_s_Garden_of_Verses">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6401606-goldgato?shelf=spring">spring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6401606-goldgato?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6401606-goldgato?shelf=children">children</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer292272563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13121592301723112741">Stevenson can not simply sit quietly on a shelf. His works beg to be lifted and opened for new worlds to discover. As a child, he was lonely and ill and many of the poems in this collection for children exude that sense of isolation.<br/><br/>I'm sure everyone has their favorites, but mine was always THE LAMPLIGHTER. At my school in Melbourne, we would have a midday break of tea and biscuits, and my teacher would recite the beginning of this poem. It was Stevenson's ode to a world quickly changing, as ele</span>
  <span id="freeText13121592301723112741" style="display:none">Stevenson can not simply sit quietly on a shelf. His works beg to be lifted and opened for new worlds to discover. As a child, he was lonely and ill and many of the poems in this collection for children exude that sense of isolation.<br /><br />I'm sure everyone has their favorites, but mine was always THE LAMPLIGHTER. At my school in Melbourne, we would have a midday break of tea and biscuits, and my teacher would recite the beginning of this poem. It was Stevenson's ode to a world quickly changing, as electricity replaced gaslamps in the late 19th century.<br /><br /><i>My tea is nearly ready and the sun has left the sky</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13121592301723112741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7312859857326885683"> I must have had some version of this collection as a child as I remembered the poem “Me and My Shadow” which I still remember some of the opening lines. These poems are very nostalgic and the author's childhood appears throughout them. They are basic and simple in nature but after all they were written with children in mind. I loved reading this and taking a trip down memory lane. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3161302693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3161302693" />
    <a title="Gerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1525599-gerry"><img alt="Gerry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580749249p2/1525599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3161302693?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gerry" href="/user/show/1525599-gerry">Gerry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780751371048" href="/book/show/3047300-a-child-s-garden-of-verses">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3161302693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3766182037813407058">This is a selection of poems from Robert Louis Stevenson's charming 'A Child's Garden of Verses' and the (unacknowledged) editor states they have been chosen because they are 'the poems most appropriate for today's [1997] child'. Whilst I understand that statement I am not fully in agreement with it for all the poems in the original book appear to be suitable for a child of any generation. But, I appreciate that is a personal view so I respect what they have chosen and take it from there.<br/><br/>I am de</span>
  <span id="freeText3766182037813407058" style="display:none">This is a selection of poems from Robert Louis Stevenson's charming 'A Child's Garden of Verses' and the (unacknowledged) editor states they have been chosen because they are 'the poems most appropriate for today's [1997] child'. Whilst I understand that statement I am not fully in agreement with it for all the poems in the original book appear to be suitable for a child of any generation. But, I appreciate that is a personal view so I respect what they have chosen and take it from there.<br /><br />I am delighted to say that 'From a Railway Carriage' is one of those chosen, for the sound of the train racing along the line is captured in its opening lines, 'Faster than fairies, faster than witches,/Bridges and houses, hedges and ditches...', which seem to epitomise the sound of the train on the track. And the accompanying illustration is superb. This edition has paintings by famous artists to accompany each poem and for this one it is Derold Page, a living South African-born artist currently residing in Somerset, who provides an exquisite view of a 'Late Summer Landscape'.<br /><br />I love the brevity of 'Rain' (title and all!) and Maxime Maufra's painting of 'La Pluie, Quai de Concarneau' captures the words admirably. Similarly Adelaide Claxton's 'Wonderland' matches very well the words in another of my favourites (they all are really favourites) 'Picture-books in Winter' with its delightful last verse, 'How am I to sing your praise,/Happy Chimney-corner days,/Sitting safe in nursery nooks,/Reading picture story-books?' While I am not sitting in a nursery - some friends still say it probably is! - that is exactly what I am doing now as the rain pours down outside!<br /><br />You can tell I love Robert Louis Stevenson and this book of delightful childhood poetry with its evocative and appropriate paintings does nothing to lessen that admiration. As I have written once before 'A Child's Garden of Verses' - in any edition - is one to be read over and over again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3766182037813407058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4556555037379534958" style="display:none">What wonderful memories this little book holds! It is responsible for my bibliomania of today. We were a reading family and my parents bought me this book when I was a small child and would read to me from it until I mastered reading on my own. Such classic poems it contains and my edition has illustrations by the wonderful Jesse Wilcox Smith which makes it even better. Along with <i>Poems of Childhood</i> by Eugene Field, this book never gets old and is still enjoyable to the adult who read it as a child.<br /><br /><b>The Wind</b><br />"I saw you toss the kites on high<br />And blow the birds about the sky;<br />And all around I heard you pass,<br />Like ladies' skirts across the grass-<br />O wind, a-blowing all day long,<br />O Wind, that sings so loud a song"<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_36948169" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36948169" />
    <a title="Wayne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1466146-wayne"><img alt="Wayne" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36948169?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wayne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wayne" href="/user/show/1466146-wayne">Wayne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who has some modern children's poetry nearby as an antidote.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Wayne by: </span>
      my interest in Robert Louis
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1466146-wayne?shelf=children-s-books">children-s-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1466146-wayne?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36948169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4820417454329067331">I really tried to give this at least TWO stars, but when you're really glad you have finished a book I think that's a pretty good indication of the star rating.<br/><br/>Perhaps it might be thought that a poetry book should be read in small bites?? <br/>Yes, much poetry is dense in terms of compacted thoughts and image and metaphor. After reading one Shakespeare sonnet(reviewed) one has to gasp for breath. (What was that semi-trailer that just passed over me!??!!) An immediate reread is necessary. The syntax(w</span>
  <span id="freeText4820417454329067331" style="display:none">I really tried to give this at least TWO stars, but when you're really glad you have finished a book I think that's a pretty good indication of the star rating.<br /><br />Perhaps it might be thought that a poetry book should be read in small bites?? <br />Yes, much poetry is dense in terms of compacted thoughts and image and metaphor. After reading one Shakespeare sonnet(reviewed) one has to gasp for breath. (What was that semi-trailer that just passed over me!??!!) An immediate reread is necessary. The syntax(word order) is often a challenge in itself. But here, with Robert Louis, small bites came from an overdose of cloying sentimentality. A glucose overdose is NOT healthy!! And hence the poems lacked real substance. I can appreciate that for many this book was a lovely walk down Memory Lane. And I love that with A.A.Milne's "When We Were Very Young" (reviewed) and even taught them. As I have poems from "A Child's Garden". But not to the exclusion of modern poems for children. So I hope all fans do spread their wings!! <br /><br />Found a few old friends here in Louis' Garden, some I had no idea were penned by Robert Louis. These I had read in anthologies or isolated in story books and so much easier to digest. BUT to sit down and plough through a whole cloying, sentimental volume was just more than could be expected of anyone's digestive system. I needed a spoonful of medicine (metaphor for Reality) to help the sugar go down!!!! and there was none in sight.<br /><br />I have taught thousands of children and I don't think I have ever encountered a child like this!! "This" turns out to be a construct of himself as a child created wearing rose-coloured glasses - ill and privileged middle class, but with all the negative aspects of what it was really like to live ill and cut off whitewashed out. The archaic language added to the alienation, whereas usually I enjoy such a shift in style and vocabulary. Happily some very nice moments, but too much 'Niceness" in the end.<br /><br />I am now seeking refuge and recovery with an injection of Ted Hughes in his "Collected Poems for Children." However Hughes is writing 'for' and 'about' children, where Stevenson wrote exclusively 'about' children, or 'as' a child or once-child. Roald Dahl's children's verses may be another sedative!!<br /><br />My edition of "A Child's Garden" is a Collins hardback publication printed in the UK in 1946 with illustrations by A.H.Watson which are very nice but a bit too derivative of E.H.Shepard who did the A.A.Milne books of the 1920's. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4820417454329067331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_235115091" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/235115091" />
    <a title="Fox" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1702050-fox"><img alt="Fox" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1256254888p2/1702050.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/235115091?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fox" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fox" href="/user/show/1702050-fox">Fox</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1702050-fox?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1702050-fox?shelf=children-s-book">children-s-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1702050-fox?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1702050-fox?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer235115091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5376840965444810013">Much like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/81466.A_A__Milne' title='A.A. Milne' rel='nofollow noopener'> A. A. Milne</a>'s books of poetry on childhood, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/854076.Robert_Louis_Stevenson' title='Robert Louis Stevenson' rel='nofollow noopener'> Robert Louis Stevenson</a>'s can't help but transport us back to our youth and all of the wonders and concerns that come with it. Here gardens are transformed into battlefields and fairylands, and even a simple bed can become a ship and us the pirates that pilot it. Even simply going up to one's bedroom in the dark can contain all the terror and wonder of the much rumored Northwest Passage. It's heady stuff.<br/><br/>This book is utterly delightful, and </span>
  <span id="freeText5376840965444810013" style="display:none">Much like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/81466.A_A__Milne" title="A.A. Milne" rel="nofollow noopener"> A. A. Milne</a>'s books of poetry on childhood, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/854076.Robert_Louis_Stevenson" title="Robert Louis Stevenson" rel="nofollow noopener"> Robert Louis Stevenson</a>'s can't help but transport us back to our youth and all of the wonders and concerns that come with it. Here gardens are transformed into battlefields and fairylands, and even a simple bed can become a ship and us the pirates that pilot it. Even simply going up to one's bedroom in the dark can contain all the terror and wonder of the much rumored Northwest Passage. It's heady stuff.<br /><br />This book is utterly delightful, and only gets better with age. As children we can appreciate it for the wonder, as we are very much wrapped up in the drama and imagery of childhood. As an adult, we can be transported there and if the pitter patter of tiny feet between the pages isn't our own children, it is very much our own feet -that invisible child on the wind that we once were.<br /><br />This is a much beloved, and much deserved classic. Even as the years go on they don't dull the poignancy of this poetry. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5376840965444810013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F+DiKbPNe2cAQmTZe0PGjCHlTxusa/Wa3WKheBcQHvDrP7BHE1+SsGdYtnVLH47WYRtr6tjL+LJ54c9gILIecg==')})
    }
  }

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Beginning with stories of heroes from British history, including King Alfred and the Cakes, King Canute on the Seashore, and Bruce and the Spider, the book moves on to tales of other lands. From Ancient Greece come stories of The Brave Three Hundred, Alexander and Bucepahlus, and Diogenes the Wise Man. Introducing the history of Rome are the Story of Cincinnatus, Horatius at the Bridge, and Julius Caesar. The stories of William Tell, Arnold Winkelried, and Robin Hood impart a bit of the flavor of the Middle Ages. Rounding out the collection are a number of timeless tales that show heroes in action: Damon and Pythias, The Sword of Damocles, Picciola, and The King and His Hawk.Children naturally take a deep interest in such stories. The reading of them will not only give pleasure but will help to lay the foundation for broader literary studies since nearly all are the subjects of frequent allusions in poetry and prose. <span id="freeTextContainer15891484735063033296">Robert Louis Balfour Stevenson was a Scottish novelist, poet, and travel writer, and a leading representative of English literature. He was greatly admired by many authors, including Jorge Luis Borges, Ernest Hemingway, Rudyard Kipling and Vladimir Nabokov.<br/><br/>Most modernist writers dismissed him, however, because he was popular and did not write within their narrow definition of literature. It is onl</span>
  <span id="freeText15891484735063033296" style="display:none">Robert Louis Balfour Stevenson was a Scottish novelist, poet, and travel writer, and a leading representative of English literature. He was greatly admired by many authors, including Jorge Luis Borges, Ernest Hemingway, Rudyard Kipling and Vladimir Nabokov.<br /><br />Most modernist writers dismissed him, however, because he was popular and did not write within their narrow definition of literature. It is only recently that critics have begun to look beyond Stevenson's popularity and allow him a place in the Western canon.</span>
